Update Feb 2021 - This location is now closed! :(

I had a great experience here and so glad I discovered a location in SD because I was going to LA and Texas to get my Rainbow shopping on! It's a large store with a variety of clothing and well stocked on the footwear.  There are no fitting rooms but you can try on items over your clothes. I found some cute pieces and realized everything sold online is not in the stores.  You can take a chance and purchase online and if you don't like it, return it to your nearest Rainbow.  Now my #1 go to store to shop!< /text>

< review>
My fiance and I have been staying here for almost a month as we are waiting for our apartment to be ready. We have 2 well-trained, well-behaved, friendly service animals. They are a Husky mix and under 2 years old. Some time after I paid this morning, I received a call in my room from the manager, Sal, saying that we would have to check out  in the morning that they were not going to extend our stay anymore because it was brought to his attention that we had dogs in our room. I said "yes, they are service animals". He said , "well unfortunately we are not going to be able to extend your stay. You should have told us in the beginning."

Well, Sal, per the law I do NOT have to tell you ahead of time that I have service animals. Kicking us out because we have service animals is discrimination. What you are saying is that I have to tell you about my disability ahead of time in order to stay in  your establishment. If my dogs were a wheelchair, would the same apply? If my dogs were a home health aide, would I have to tell you about him/her ahead of time? So why do I have to tell  you that I have service animals ahead of time? According to the American Disabilities Act, no such notice is required and it is unlawful for you to kick me out because of my service animals and because I didn't give you advance notice I was checking in with them.

We are also Platinum Wyndham Rewards Members. You would think that being Platinum members (when Diamond is the only level left) of your loyalty program, your company would show a little more loyalty and not just discard us like yesterday's news. Obviously we have been spending money here to get to that level. I am extremely dismayed at being treated in such a manner. I expect such treatment from the dirt-bag motel down the street but I did not expect it from an establishment with the Wyndham name, especially since you boast "SERVICE ANIMALS ARE WELCOME" for all your hotels! That really should read "SERVICE ANIMALS ARE WELCOME ONLY IF YOU GET OUR PERMISSION IN ADVANCE TO HAVE ONE". Your company is too big, too well-known for you to be this ignorant of the laws and to actively participate in discrimination against anyone particularly of the disabled. I'm ashamed of you and will pursue this issue as far as I need to .

In addition, the front desk prior to this had informed us that it was coming up on 28 days that we had been staying here. Hotels try to do this to circumvent the law that would give one tenancy if staying in the hotel for 30 consecutive days because if you check out and then check back in the next day, you have to wait another 30 days to get tenant rights. If you move out every 28 days, you never achieve tenancy. This game that your hotel, along with several other hotels, is playing  is illegal and could result in your hotel being fined $500 each time it does this. $500 does not sound like a lot once but if everyone who you did it to came forward, I imagine it would add up to some hefty fines.

So I will not remain silent. I will tell whoever will listen that Days Inn in Carlsbad on 3700 Pio Pico Dr. participates in the "musical rooms" game to try to circumvent the tenancy law, WHICH IS ILLEGAL and they are also discriminatory, kicking people out because of known service animals brought into their establishment WHICH IS ALSO ILLEGAL.

You guys have some explaining to do!< /review>

I am giving this hotel 2 stars because the cleaning staff to a good job keeping old rooms presentable. The front staff was also nice. The continental breakfast was just okay. Would have like a bagel and fruit, which they only had apples that did not look so fresh.
The parking lot setup pretty much left a lot to be desired and was designed horribly.  One entrance to get to the one elevator. Which is not fun loaded down with bags. I guess par for the course when the hotel is as small as this one was.
I don't get why so many hotels do not have an exhaust fan. With two people taking warm showers every day for 4 days,  our clothes started smelling moist. Even with keeping used clothing separate.
The bathroom is for short people. I am 5'6" and the shower head was maybe an inch or two above my head. So if you are tall and that bugs you, something to consider.

Oh and careful with shutting the doors, they are not self closing like a lot of hotels I have stayed at before.<//review>

The short ribs are some of the better prepared slices I've had in this town - NO BONES! And a big portion!  The second time, I had the noodles, nicely spiced and filling.  I'll be back to try more.  I tried my friend's sweet potato fries and those were VERY tasty.  Next time I'm getting some of those for myself.< /Text>

< review>
I just went there tonight on a whim. I tried the crispy egg rolls and they were delicious! Meaty too, not just tons of cabbage in there, and very crispy, served on a place with lettuce, mint, and a nice dish of fish sauce.

Very nice people too! The proprietress and I discussed the smell of firecrackers on Chinese New Year (I love it, she's not a fan lol) and while we talked, the proprietor had my egg rolls all fried and ready sooner than expected.

I can see this place is going to be a "go-to" place that matches well with the coffee shop next door.

<Review>This place is really quaint, but with a rustic feel. They offer a great fresh juice menu, and well as ready-made cold-pressed juices. The staff is very friendly, accommodating, and knowledgeable.

I ran into here when I landed in LA, because I felt a sniffle on the plane, and I rarely get sick. I took a spicy lemon juice shot, and tried their Green #3 cold-pressed bottle. Although I was too late in my efforts, and my cold overtook me, I went back the next day for another shot, and had them whip me up a fresh juice blend. I also ordered a fruit bowl that had strawberries, acai, bananas and coconut, and I wish I could tell you how it tasted, but I was stuffed up too bad. But I will tell you that it looked delicious!

The next day, I was almost good as new, and if I would have had time to go back again before I had to fly back to Chicago, I would have. Thanks Juice Crafters, I know if I didn't find you, my cold would have lasted longer, and I appreciate that you supplied the cure!</Review></record>

<Review>I feel obligated to write this review based on my own experience, because I was misled by the good reviews here.

My old onlay (similar to a crown) fractured recently and my previous dentist unfortunately passed away, so I had to look for a new one. I went to this dental office because of their 5 star Yelp/Google reviews. What a mistake. The new onlay I got from them was a bad fit with gaps and sensitivities. In addition, the procedure caused three painful mouth sores on my gums. Now I have to go to another dentist to have it redone.

They have a CEREC machine that can make an onlay or crown in 2 hours. I was skeptical but the dentist assured me that the fit should be more precise than the traditional lab-made one. It is not.

Just as most reviews have already mentioned, their dentists are nice individuals. So are the front desk team and dental hygienists. But what I need the most for my onlay are hard dental skills and attention to detail, which unfortunately are what they lack.
